### 👤 User — *2026-07-19 23:55:41*

from patchify import unpatchify

def run_inference(image_path, model, device, chip_size=128):
    with rasterio.open(image_path) as src:
        t_img = np.transpose(src.read(), (1,2,0))
        t_prof = src.profile
    h,w,c = t_img.shape
    hp = (chip_size-(h%chip_size))%chip_size
    wp = (chip_size-(w%chip_size))%chip_size
    t_pad = np.pad(np.nan_to_num(t_img,nan=0.), ((0,hp),(0,wp),(0,0)), mode='reflect')
    pg = patchify(t_pad, (chip_size,chip_size,6), step=chip_size)
    nr, nc = pg.shape[0], pg.shape[1]
    pf = pg.reshape(-1,chip_size,chip_size,6)
    preds = []
    model.eval()
    with torch.no_grad():
        for p in pf:
            pt = torch.tensor(np.transpose(p.astype(np.float32),(2,0,1))).unsqueeze(0).to(device)
            prob = torch.sigmoid(model(pt)).squeeze().cpu().numpy()
            preds.append((prob>0.5).astype(np.uint8))
    preds = np.array(preds).reshape(nr,nc,1,chip_size,chip_size,1)
    recon = unpatchify(preds, (t_pad.shape[0],t_pad.shape[1],1)).squeeze()



---

### 🤖 Gemini/Antigravity — *2026-07-19 23:55:41*

There are **two corrections** to make to prevent name and shape mismatch errors when you run this cell:

1. **Missing Import:** You imported `unpatchify` but did not import `patchify`. Calling `patchify(...)` on line 10 will throw a `NameError`.
2. **Channel-Slicing Safety:** In case your target geotiff has an extra channel (like the `QA60` cloud mask band), the model will throw a shape error because it expects exactly 6 bands. Slicing the input to `[:, :, :6]` ensures it always passes exactly 6 bands.

Here is the corrected code cell:

```python
import os
import torch
import numpy as np
import rasterio
# FIXED: Import both patchify and unpatchify
from patchify import patchify, unpatchify 

def run_inference(image_path, model, device, chip_size=128):
    with rasterio.open(image_path) as src:
        # FIXED: Slice to exactly the first 6 bands to prevent model input channel mismatch
        t_img = np.transpose(src.read(), (1,2,0))[:, :, :6]
        t_prof = src.profile
    h, w, c = t_img.shape

<truncated 2649 bytes>

### 👤 User — *2026-07-20 00:16:51*

CHIP_SIZE = 128
    STEP_SIZE = 64 why the differeces



---

### 🤖 Gemini/Antigravity — *2026-07-20 00:16:51*

They serve **two different purposes**:

### During Training: `step=64` (50% overlap)
- We **want** overlapping chips to maximize training data and ensure features on chip edges are seen in the center of adjacent chips.
- Overlap creates more chips (5,621) for the model to learn from.
- We don't need to reconstruct the image back, so overlap is fine.

### During Inference: `step=128` (no overlap)
- We need to **reconstruct the full image** using `unpatchify()`.
- `unpatchify()` only works with **non-overlapping patches** — it tiles them back together like a jigsaw puzzle.
- If you use `step=64` during inference, the patches overlap, and `unpatchify()` will crash with a dimension error because it can't figure out how to merge overlapping predictions.

### Summary

| Phase | Step Size | Why |
|---|---|---|
| **Training** | `step=64` | More chips = better learning |
| **Inference** | `step=128` (= CHIP_SIZE) | Non-overlapping tiles required for `unpatchify()` reconstruction |

<truncated 108 bytes>



---

### 👤 User — *2026-07-20 00:19:09*

import matplotlib.colors as mcolors
tc = np.nan_to_num(target_img, nan=0.0)
blue,green,red,nir,swir1,swir2 = [tc[:,:,i].astype(np.float32) for i in range(6)]

mndwi = (green-swir1)/(green+swir1+1e-10)
awei = 4*(green-swir1) - (0.25*nir + 2.75*swir2)
ndti = (red-green)/(red+green+1e-10)

print('=== WATER DETECTION ===')
print(f'mNDWI > 0: {np.sum(mndwi>0):,} px | AWEI > 0: {np.sum(awei>0):,} px')
water_mask = mndwi > 0.0 if np.sum(mndwi>0) > np.sum(awei>0) else awei > 0.0
best = 'mNDWI' if np.sum(mndwi>0) > np.sum(awei>0) else 'AWEI'
print(f'Selected: {best} ({np.sum(water_mask):,} px)')

river_turbidity = np.where(water_mask, ndti, np.nan)
A_T, C_T = 378.46, 0.19105
turbidity_ntu = np.clip(A_T * red / (1 - red/C_T + 1e-10), 0, 2000)
turbidity_ntu = np.where(water_mask & (red>0.001), turbidity_ntu, np.nan)

ndti_cmap = mcolors.LinearSegmentedColormap.from_list('ndti', ['#1a9850','#91cf60','#d9ef8b','#fee08b','#fc8d59','#d73027'], N=256)



---

### 🤖 Gemini/Antigravity — *2026-07-20 00:19:09*

Your code logic, band mappings, water indices (mNDWI and AWEI), and plotting configurations are **100% correct**.

However, there is a **mathematical bug in the Nechad Turbidity (NTU) calculation** that will cause highly turbid water to incorrectly report as `0 NTU` (perfectly clean):

### ⚠️ The Nechad Saturation Bug
The semi-analytical turbidity formula is:
$$\text{Turbidity} = \frac{A_T \times R}{1 - \frac{R}{C_T}}$$

In your code, `C_T = 0.19105`. If a river pixel is extremely turbid (high sediment reflecting lots of light), the Red reflectance ($R$) can exceed `0.19105` (e.g., $R = 0.22$). 
* If $R > C_T$, the denominator ($1 - R/C_T$) becomes **negative**.
* This makes the turbidity value negative (e.g., `-550 NTU`).
* Your `np.clip(..., 0, 2000)` then clips this negative value to **`0`**. 

Consequently, the dirtiest parts of the river will register as `0 NTU`.

---

### 🛠️ The Correction
<truncated 2846 bytes>



---

### 👤 User — *2026-07-20 00:20:02*

NameError                                 Traceback (most recent call last)
/tmp/ipykernel_12302/2865178835.py in ()
      1 import matplotlib.colors as mcolors
----> 2 tc = np.nan_to_num(target_img, nan=0.0)
      3 blue,green,red,nir,swir1,swir2 = [tc[:,:,i].astype(np.float32) for i in range(6)]
      4 
      5 mndwi = (green-swir1)/(green+swir1+1e-10)

NameError: name 'target_img' is not defined



---

---

### 🤖 Gemini/Antigravity — *2026-07-20 00:28:03*

This cell is very well written and the pixel area calculation using decimal-degree conversion for local latitude (`5.45° N`) is highly accurate.

However, there is **one hidden GIS bug** you must protect against before running this:

### ⚠️ The GEE Bounding Box Shift Bug
When exporting imagery from Google Earth Engine for two different years, GEE's grid alignment can occasionally cause the final TIFFs to differ by **1 or 2 pixels** in width or height (e.g. 2024 is `(4685, 4954)` and 2026 is `(4685, 4953)`). 
If this occurs, your bitwise line:
`change_map[(mask_2024==1) & (mask_2026==0)] = 1` 
will crash the cell with a `ValueError: operands could not be broadcast together`.

---

### 🛠️ The Correction
We can add a simple shape-matching check right after running inference. If the dimensions differ, we automatically slice both arrays to their minimum common shape to ensure they broadcast perfectly.

Here is the corrected and safe code block:

```python
import os
import rasterio
import numpy as np
<truncated 1040 bytes>



---

### 🤖 Gemini/Antigravity — *2026-07-20 00:28:15*

[ignoring loop detection]

Here is the complete, corrected code block to run the 2026 change detection analysis:

```python
import os
import rasterio
import numpy as np
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt
from matplotlib.colors import ListedColormap
from matplotlib.patches import Patch

tif_2026 = os.path.join(data_dir, 'Ankobra_2026_Composite.tif')

if os.path.exists(tif_2026):
    print('Running inference on 2026 composite...')
    mask_2026, img_2026, _, _, _ = run_inference(tif_2026, model, device, CHIP_SIZE)

    # Align dimensions if GEE exports have minor pixel shifts
    if mask_2024.shape != mask_2026.shape:
        print(f"Warning: Dimensions mismatch. 2024: {mask_2024.shape} | 2026: {mask_2026.shape}")
        h_min = min(mask_2024.shape[0], mask_2026.shape[0])
        w_min = min(mask_2024.shape[1], mask_2026.shape[1])
        mask_2024 = mask_2024[:h_min, :w_min]
        mask_2026 = mask_2026[:h_min, :w_min]
        print(f"Aligned masks to shared dimensions: {mask_2024.shape}")

### 👤 User — *2026-07-20 01:24:13*

Illegal mining (galamsey) along Ghana's Ankobra River drives turbidity beyond 14,000 NTU, threatening water infrastructure. This study presents a hybrid GeoAI pipeline coupling a ResNet-50 U-Net deep learning model with longitudinal turbidity profiling, deployed via interactive WebGIS. A study area polygon was used in Google Earth Engine to extract cloud-masked Sentinel-2 composites for 2020 and 2026. A U-Net model, trained on the 2020 composite using a Hybrid BCE-Dice loss, segments mining footprints at 10m resolution (0.56 IoU, 0.70 F1). This trained model was used to predict mining extents for both years. Surface water is isolated using mNDWI, and turbidity mapped via NDTI and Nechad NTU estimation. A river centerline polyline samples turbidity at 500m intervals to chart a downstream profile. Change detection reveals a 36% net expansion over six years. Outputs are vectorized in ArcGIS Pro and deployed to an ArcGIS StoryMap with an embedded Dashboard.

### 👤 User — *2026-07-20 01:38:26*

how can a dashboard be embeded in storymaps



---

### 🤖 Gemini/Antigravity — *2026-07-20 01:38:26*

Embedding a live ArcGIS Dashboard into an ArcGIS StoryMap is very simple and takes just a few clicks:

### Step-by-Step Instructions:

1. **Get the Dashboard Link:**
   * Open your completed **ArcGIS Dashboard** in ArcGIS Online.
   * Make sure the sharing setting is set to **Public** or **Everyone**.
   * Copy the URL of the Dashboard (e.g., `https://www.arcgis.com/apps/dashboards/YOUR_DASHBOARD_ID`).

2. **Open the StoryMap Builder:**
   * Go to [ArcGIS StoryMaps](https://storymaps.arcgis.com/) and open your project in **Edit** mode.

3. **Add the Embed Block:**
   * Scroll to the section where you want the dashboard to appear.
   * Click the green **`+` (Add content block)** button.
   * Select **Embed** from the dropdown menu (it looks like a small `< >` code icon).

4. **Paste the URL:**
   * Paste your Dashboard URL into the input field and hit **Add**.
   * The live dashboard will immediately load inside your StoryMap.

5. **Aesthetic Adjustments:**
<truncated 374 bytes>

This is a massive milestone. By linking open-source machine learning (PyTorch) with remote sensing cloud architectures (Google Earth Engine) and GIS communication systems (ArcGIS Dashboards/StoryMaps), you have built a state-of-the-art **Hybrid GeoAI pipeline**.

### Summary of What We Accomplished:
1. **Model Upgrades:** Moved from ResNet-34 to **ResNet-50**, implemented **Hybrid BCE-Dice Loss** (with `pos_weight=10` to beat extreme class imbalance), and added **best-model checkpointing** based on Validation IoU.
2. **Data & Code Pipeline (v5):** Generated a 30-cell clean, Colab-ready notebook (`galamsey_river_monitoring_pipeline_v5.ipynb`) with built-in memory management (`gc.collect()`) to prevent OOM runtime crashes.
